This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n    20→// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n    21→//\n    22→// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n    23→// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n    24→// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n    25→// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n    26→// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n    27→// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n    28→// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n    29→//\n    30→// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n    31→// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n    32→// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n    33→// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n    34→// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n    35→// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n    36→// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n    37→//\n    38→// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n    39→// cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n    40→// this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n    41→// availability.\n    42→//\n    43→// Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n    44→// taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n    45→// should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n    46→// until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n    47→// when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n    48→// to master availability.\n    49→//\n    50→// DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n    51→// or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\n    52→// your own risk.\n    53→package leaderelection\n    54→\n    55→import (\n    56→\t\"bytes\"\n    57→\t\"context\"\n    58→\t\"fmt\"\n    59→\t\"sync\"\n    60→\t\"time\"\n    61→\n    62→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors\"\n    63→\tmetav1 \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1\"\n    64→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n    65→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n    66→\trl \"k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock\"\n    67→\t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n    68→\t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n    69→)\n    70→\n    71→const (\n    72→\tJitterFactor = 1.2\n    73→)\n    74→\n    75→// NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\n    76→func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\n    77→\tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\n    78→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than renewDeadline\")\n    79→\t}\n    80→\tif lec.RenewDeadline <= time.Duration(JitterFactor*float64(lec.RetryPeriod)) {\n    81→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than retryPeriod*JitterFactor\")\n    82→\t}\n    83→\tif lec.LeaseDuration < 1 {\n    84→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than zero\")\n    85→\t}\n    86→\tif lec.RenewDeadline < 1 {\n    87→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than zero\")\n    88→\t}\n    89→\tif lec.RetryPeriod < 1 {\n    90→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"retryPeriod must be greater than zero\")\n    91→\t}\n    92→\tif lec.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading == nil {\n    93→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStartedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n    94→\t}\n    95→\tif lec.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading == nil {\n    96→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStoppedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n    97→\t}\n    98→\n    99→\tif lec.Lock == nil {\n   100→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock must not be nil.\")\n   101→\t}\n   102→\tid := lec.Lock.Identity()\n   103→\tif id == \"\" {\n   104→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock identity is empty\")\n   105→\t}\n   106→\n   107→\tle := LeaderElector{\n   108→\t\tconfig:  lec,\n   109→\t\tclock:   clock.RealClock{},\n   110→\t\tmetrics: globalMetricsFactory.newLeaderMetrics(),\n   111→\t}\n   112→\tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n   113→\treturn &le, nil\n   114→}\n   115→\n   116→type LeaderElectionConfig struct {\n   117→\t// Lock is the resource that will be used for locking\n   118→\tLock rl.Interface\n   119→\n   120→\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\n   121→\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\n   122→\t// last observed ack.\n   123→\t//\n   124→\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\n   125→\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\n   126→\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\n   127→\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\n   128→\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\n   129→\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\n   130→\t// long waits in the scenario.\n   131→\t//\n   132→\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\n   133→\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\n   134→\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\n   135→\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\n   136→\t//\n   137→\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\n   138→\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\n   139→\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\n   140→\t// between tries of actions.\n   141→\t//\n   142→\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\n   143→\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\n   144→\n   145→\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\n   146→\t// events of the LeaderElector\n   147→\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\n   148→\n   149→\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\n   150→\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\n   151→\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\n   152→\n   153→\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\n   154→\t// when the run context is cancelled. If you set this to true, you must\n   155→\t// ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n   156→\t// prior to cancelling the context, or you may have two processes\n   157→\t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n   158→\tReleaseOnCancel bool\n   159→\n   160→\t// Name is the name of the resource lock for debugging\n   161→\tName string\n   162→\n   163→\t// Coordinated will use the Coordinated Leader Election feature\n   164→\t// WARNING: Coordinated leader election is ALPHA.\n   165→\tCoordinated bool\n   166→}\n   167→\n   168→// LeaderCallbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain\n   169→// lifecycle events of the LeaderElector. These are invoked asynchronously.\n   170→//\n   171→// possible future callbacks:\n   172→//   - OnChallenge()\n   173→type LeaderCallbacks struct {\n   174→\t// OnStartedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client starts leading\n   175→\tOnStartedLeading func(context.Context)\n   176→\t// OnStoppedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client stops leading.\n   177→\t// This callback is always called when the LeaderElector exits, even if it did not start leading.\n   178→\t// Users should not assume that OnStoppedLeading is only called after OnStartedLeading.\n   179→\t// see: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/127675#discussion_r1780059887\n   180→\tOnStoppedLeading func()\n   181→\t// OnNewLeader is called when the client observes a leader that is\n   182→\t// not the previously observed leader. This includes the first observed\n   183→\t// leader when the client starts.\n   184→\tOnNewLeader func(identity string)\n   185→}\n   186→\n   187→// LeaderElector is a leader election client.\n   188→type LeaderElector struct {\n   189→\tconfig LeaderElectionConfig\n   190→\t// internal bookkeeping\n   191→\tobservedRecord    rl.LeaderElectionRecord\n   192→\tobservedRawRecord []byte\n   193→\tobservedTime      time.Time\n   194→\t// used to implement OnNewLeader(), may lag slightly from the\n   195→\t// value observedRecord.HolderIdentity if the transition has\n   196→\t// not yet been reported.\n   197→\treportedLeader string\n   198→\n   199→\t// clock is wrapper around time to allow for less flaky testing\n   200→\tclock clock.Clock\n   201→\n   202→\t// used to lock the observedRecord and the observedTime\n   203→\tobservedRecordLock sync.RWMutex\n   204→\n   205→\tmetrics leaderMetricsAdapter\n   206→}\n   207→\n   208→// Run starts the leader election loop. Run will not return\n   209→// before leader election loop is stopped by ctx or it has\n   210→// stopped holding the leader lease\n   211→func (le *LeaderElector) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n   212→\tdefer runtime.HandleCrashWithContext(ctx)\n   213→\tdefer le.config.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading()\n   214→\n   215→\tif !le.acquire(ctx) {\n   216→\t\treturn // ctx signalled done\n   217→\t}\n   218→\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n   219→\tdefer cancel()\n   220→\tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading(ctx)\n   221→\tle.renew(ctx)\n   222→}\n   223→\n   224→// RunOrDie starts a client with the provided config or panics if the config\n   225→// fails to validate. last observed leader was this client else returns false.\n   246→func (le *LeaderElector) IsLeader() bool {\n   247→\treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity == le.config.Lock.Identity()\n   248→}\n   249→\n   250→// acquire loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns true immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew succeeds.\n   251→// Returns false if ctx signals done.\n   252→func (le *LeaderElector) acquire(ctx context.Context) bool {\n   253→\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n   254→\tdefer cancel()\n   255→\tsucceeded := false\n   256→\tdesc := le.config.Lock.Describe()\n   257→\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   258→\tlogger.Info(\"Attempting to acquire leader lease...\", \"lock\", desc)\n   259→\twait.JitterUntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n 274→\t}, le.config.RetryPeriod, JitterFactor, true)\n   275→\treturn succeeded\n   276→}\n   277→\n   278→// renew loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew fails or ctx signals done.\n   279→func (le *LeaderElector) renew(ctx context.Context) {\n   280→\tdefer le.config.Lock.RecordEvent(\"stopped leading\")\n   281→\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n   282→\tdefer cancel()\n   283→\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   284→\twait.UntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n   285→\t\terr := wait.PollUntilContextTimeout(ctx, when immediate=true.\n   287→\t\t\t// Short-circuit this to prevent unnecessary processing and error log messages.\n   288→\t\t\tif err := ctx.Err(); err != nil {\n   289→\t\t\t\treturn false, err\n   290→\t\t\t}\n   291→\t\t\tif !le.config.Coordinated {\n   292→\t\t\t\treturn le.tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx), nil\n   293→\t\t\t} else {\n   294→\t\t\t\treturn le.tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx), nil\n   295→\t\t\t}\n   296→\t\t})\n   297→\t\tle.maybeReportTransition()\n   298→\t\tdesc := le.config.Lock.Describe()\n   299→\t\tif err == nil {\n   300→\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Successfully renewed lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n   301→\t\t\treturn\n   302→\t\t}\n   303→\t\tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n   304→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Failed to renew lease\", \"lock\", desc, \"err\", err)\n   305→\t\tcancel()\n   306→\t}, le.config.RetryPeriod)\n   307→\n   308→\t// if we hold the lease, give it up\n   309→\tif le.config.ReleaseOnCancel {\n   310→\t\tle.release(logger)\n   311→\t}\n Returns true on success else returns\n   351→// false.\n   352→func (le *LeaderElector) tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx context.Context) bool {\n   353→\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   354→\tnow := metav1.NewTime(le.clock.Now())\n   355→\tleaderElectionRecord := rl.LeaderElectionRecord{\n   356→\t\tHolderIdentity:       le.config.Lock.Identity(),\n   357→\t\tLeaseDurationSeconds: int(le.config.LeaseDuration / time.Second),\n   358→\t\tRenewTime:            now,\n   359→\t\tAcquireTime:          now,\n   360→\t}\n   361→\n   362→\t// 1. obtain the electionRecord\n   363→\toldLeaderElectionRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord, err := le.config.Lock.Get(ctx)\n   364→\tif err != nil {\n   365→\t\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\n   366→\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Error retrieving lease lock\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n   367→\t\t\treturn false\n   368→\t\t}\n   369→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Lease lock not found\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe(), \"err\", err)\n   370→\t\treturn false\n   371→\t}\n   372→\n   373→\t// 2. 98→// PeerEndpointController is the controller manager for updating the peer endpoint leases.\n    99→// This provides a separate independent reconciliation loop for peer endpoint leases\n   100→// which ensures that the peer kube-apiservers are fetching the updated endpoint info for a given apiserver\n   101→// in the case when the peer wants to proxy the request to the given apiserver because it can not serve the\n   102→// request itself due to version mismatch.\n   103→type PeerEndpointLeaseController struct {\n   104→\treconciler       PeerEndpointLeaseReconciler\n   105→\tendpointInterval time.Duration\n   106→\tserverId         string\n   107→\t// peeraddress stores the IP and port of this kube-apiserver. {\"repo\": \"etcd-io/etcd\", \"path\": \"client/v3/concurrency/election.go\", \"symbol\": \"Resign\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Leader Election Patterns: Kubernetes vs etcd\\n\\n### Kubernetes: Lease-Based Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election through a distributed lease mechanism that operates independently of the control plane's etcd backend consensus. The core implementation is in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`, which provides the `LeaderElector` type that manages the acquisition and renewal of leases.\\n\\n**Core Mechanism:**\\nThe `LeaderElector` type in `leaderelection.go` implements a client-side leader election protocol with configurable timing: a default lease duration of 15 seconds, renewal deadline of 10 seconds, and retry period of 2 seconds. The main `Run()` function orchestrates a continuous loop that attempts to acquire or renew leadership using the `tryAcquireOrRenew()` function. Leadership is stored in Kubernetes `Lease` objects, which act as distributed locks.\\n\\n**Lease-Based Lock Implementation:**\\nThe `LeaseLock` type in `resourcelock/leaselock.go` implements the `Interface` defined in `resourcelock/interface.go`. It stores election metadata in the Lease resource's spec field, including `HolderIdentity` (current leader), `LeaseDurationSeconds`, `AcquireTime`, `RenewTime`, and `LeaderTransitions` count. The `LeaderElectionRecord` structure encapsulates these fields.\\n\\n**Failover and Re-election:**\\nWhen the current leader fails to renew its lease within the `RenewDeadline` (10 seconds), the lease expires after the `LeaseDuration` (15 seconds). Non-leader instances detect this expiry and attempt acquisition. The `isLeaseExpired()` function in `election.go` checks if the current time exceeds `RenewTime + LeaseDurationSeconds`. Upon failover, any remaining candidate can acquire the lease and become leader.\\n\\n**Coordinated Election Mode:**\\nKubernetes also implements an optional coordinated election strategy using `LeaseCandidate` objects in `leasecandidate.go`. The `Controller` in `leaderelection_controller.go` runs the `reconcileElectionStep()` function, which periodically (every 5 seconds) sends ping times to registered candidates and collects their acknowledgments. The controller then invokes `pickBestLeaderOldestEmulationVersion()` from `election.go` to select the best candidate based on emulation version (backward compatibility) and binary version. This graceful approach prefers older, more stable nodes for leadership, with a 30-minute validity window for candidates enforced by the `LeaseCandidateGCController` in `leasecandidategc_controller.go`.\\n\\n**API Server Peer Discovery:**\\nThe `PeerEndpointLeaseController` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/reconcilers/peer_endpoint_lease.go` uses a similar lease mechanism to register API server endpoints, enabling peer discovery during version skew scenarios.\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd uses the Raft consensus algorithm for leader election, where leadership is determined by Raft's quorum-based election mechanism rather than distributed locks. The core Raft implementation is in `server/etcdserver/raft.go`.\\n\\n**Raft Leader Detection:**\\nThe `raftNode` type in `raft.go` wraps the Raft state machine. The `start()` function processes Raft ready states, monitoring `SoftState.Lead` to detect leadership changes. When `rd.SoftState.Lead != raft.None`, a new leader has been elected, triggering calls to the `updateLeadership` callback. This detection is automatic and quorum-based—no explicit leases are required.\\n\\n**Server-Side Leadership Management:**\\nThe `EtcdServer` type in `server/etcdserver/server.go` provides leadership query functions: `Lead()` returns the current leader ID as a uint64, `Leader()` returns it as a `types.ID`, and `isLeader()` checks if the local node is the leader. The `setLead()` and `getLead()` functions atomically manage the leader ID. The `ensureLeadership()` function performs a linearizable read to verify the current member still holds leadership.\\n\\n**Automatic Failover:**\\nWhen a leader fails, the Raft algorithm automatically triggers an election timeout. Remaining members detect the leader's absence and initiate an election where a new leader is chosen by Raft consensus. The `advanceTicks()` function in `raft.go` adjusts election timing for multi-datacenter deployments, preventing unnecessary frequent elections during network latency.\\n\\n**Graceful Leadership Transfer:**\\nThe `MoveLeader()` function in `server.go` explicitly transfers leadership to a specified node. It validates the transferee is not a learner and calls `s.r.TransferLeadership()` from the underlying Raft library. The transfer polls `s.Lead()` until the transfer completes or times out. The `TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown()` function gracefully transfers leadership on shutdown, using `longestConnected()` from `util.go` to identify the most reliable candidate—the member with the oldest \\\"active-since\\\" connection time.\\n\\n**Member Health Tracking:**\\nThe `Transporter` interface in `api/rafthttp/transport.go` provides `ActiveSince(id types.ID)` to return when a peer was last successfully contacted. The `longestConnected()` utility uses this to find members with stable, long-lived connections, making them preferred leadership transfer targets.\\n\\n**Failover Testing:**\\nEnd-to-end and integration tests in `tests/e2e/failover_test.go` and `tests/integration/v3_failover_test.go` validate failover behavior during defragmentation, server shutdowns, and cluster operations.\\n\\n**Client-Side Election:**\\nFor application-level leader election, etcd provides the `Election` type in `client/v3/concurrency/election.go`. Applications call `Campaign()` to enter the election, `Resign()` to step down, and `Observe()` to watch for leader changes. This is separate from the server's Raft-based leadership and is built on top of etcd's key-value storage and leasing mechanisms.\\n\\n**Leadership Transfer CLI:**\\nThe `move_leader_command.go` in etcdctl provides the `move-leader` command, allowing operators to manually trigger leadership transfers. It finds the current leader via Status RPC and validates the target member before calling the client's `MoveLeader()` RPC.\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Consensus Mechanism:** Kubernetes uses explicit lease-based election independent of its backing store; etcd uses Raft's built-in consensus for server leadership.\\n2. **Timing:** Kubernetes leases have explicit duration timers (15s lease, 10s renewal deadline); Raft uses election timeouts (customizable via configuration).\\n3. **Failover Speed:** Kubernetes requires lease expiry time (up to 15s); Raft typically elects a new leader within one election timeout (typically 150-300ms).\\n4. **Transfer Strategy:** Kubernetes coordinated mode prefers stable (older version) nodes; etcd prefers the longest-connected node.\\n5. **Graceful Shutdown:** Kubernetes controls its own graceful transitions via `PreferredHolder`; etcd uses Raft's `TransferLeadership()` mechanism.\\n6. **Client API:** Kubernetes leader election is internal to control plane components; etcd exposes client-side election through the gRPC election service in `api/v3election/election.go`.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":7772,"cache_read_input_tokens":20996,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":7772},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"d2ef3d65-ba57-4503-a2bc-e5bf6c8dad04","uuid":"a2586171-1f88-484c-bba2-722f1dc3b648"}
